                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">فَضْلٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [an inf. n.: (see 1, throughout:) and also a simple subst., signifying] <hi rend="ital">An exceeding, a redundant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a superfluous, quantum</hi> [of anything, good or evil]; <hi rend="ital">an excess, a redundance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a superfluity;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">زِيَادَةٌ</foreign>; (Mgh, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَقْصٌ</foreign>: (S, O, K:) [and often meaning <hi rend="ital">superabundance,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exuberance;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">surpassingness, superiority,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">excellence.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى غَيْرِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">over another,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">others, than him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">preponderance:</hi>] the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">فُضُولٌ</foreign> (Mgh, Msb, K:) and this is sometimes used as a sing.; (Er-Rághib, Msb;) and [thus used] relates to a thing [or quality] in which is no good; (Er-Rághib, Mgh, Msb;) by a predominant application; whence the saying <foreign lang="ar">فُضُولٌ بِلَا فَضْلٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">excess without excellence</hi>]; (Mgh;) and hence the rel. n.   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n34080-1" target="فُضُولِىٌّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n34090"/></foreign> is formed from it: (Er-Rághib, Msb, TA;) [see this last word, one of the explanations of which shows that a particular meaning of <foreign lang="ar">فُضُولٌ</foreign> is the <hi rend="ital">quality of busying oneself with that which does not concern him:</hi>] accord. to Er-Rághib, <foreign lang="ar">فَضْلٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">an excess</hi> [in respect of a property or quality, or of an acquisition,] <hi rend="ital">above moderateness;</hi> and this is of two sorts; such as is commended, as the <foreign lang="ar">فضل</foreign> of knowledge, or science ; and such as is discommended, as the <foreign lang="ar">فصل</foreign> of anger at that whereat it is not necessary: but <foreign lang="ar">فَضَلٌ</foreign> is more used in relation to that which is commended; and [the pl.] <foreign lang="ar">فُضُولٌ</foreign>, in relation to that which is discommended. when the former is used of an excess [in respect of some attribute, of our of two things above the other, it is of three sorts; <foreign lang="ar">فضل</foreign> of kind, as of the animal kind above the vegetable kind; and of species, as of man above other animals; and of the individual, as of one man above another; the first and second of which three are essential attributes, such that he who is deficient in [either of] them cannot do away with his deficiency and acquire <foreign lang="ar">فضل</foreign>, as, <hi rend="ital">for instance,</hi> the horse, and the ass, which cannot acquire the excellence (<foreign lang="ar">فَضِيلَة</foreign>) of the human being; but the third may be accidental, such that the way may be found to acquire it, and of this sort are ability, wealth, rank or station, and power: and it signifies also <hi rend="ital">any gift whereof the giving to the recipient thereof is not obligatory:</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">a free gift,</hi> or gratuity; and <hi rend="ital">an act of bounty</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grace; a favour; a benefit;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">bounty</hi> as an abstract term;] as in the saying [in the Kur iv. 36], <foreign lang="ar">وَٱسْأَلُوا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهَ مِنْ فَضْلِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And ask ye God of his free gift,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of his bounty,</hi> or (as expl. in the Ksh and by Bd) <hi rend="ital">of his exhaustless treasures</hi>]; and in the saying in the Kur [v. 59 and lvii. 21 and lxii. 4], <foreign lang="ar">ذٰلِكَ فَضْلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ يُؤْتِيهِ مَنْ يَشَآءُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">That is the free gift of God; He giveth it to whom He willeth</hi>]; which comprises the three sorts of excellences (<foreign lang="ar">فَضَائِل</foreign>) [mentioned above]: thus says Er-Rághib: El-Muná- wee says, [explaining one of its meanings,] in the “ Towkeef, ” that it is the <hi rend="ital">commencing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">originating, of an act of beneficence without an efficient cause</hi> [i. e., app., <hi rend="ital">not by reason of any obligation</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">A portion remaining,</hi> (K, TA,) of a thing, such as food &amp;c., and of water in the leathern water-bag, and of wine or beverage in the vessel; (TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n34080-2" target="فَضْلَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n34082"/></foreign> and

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n34080-5" target="الفَضْلَةُ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FTO" lang="ar"/> </foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">The remaining portion</hi> of the wine or beverage [<hi rend="ital">is for the excel-lent</hi>].                   <foreign lang="ar">المَآءِ لِيُمْنَعَ بِهِ الكَلَأُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The redundance of water shall not be denied that the herbage be thereby denied</hi>]: (TA, in the present art.:) meaning that when there is a well in the desert, with herbage near it, and a person prevents others from drawing water, he thereby prevents the latter from availing themselves of the herbage; for when a man comes with his camels, and pastures them upon that herbage, and does not then water them, thirst kills them. (TA in art <foreign lang="ar">كلأ</foreign>,) And it is said in another trad., <foreign lang="ar">فَضْلُ الإِزَارِ فِى النَّارِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The redundant portion of the waist-wrapper is in the fire</hi> of Hell]; meaning what one drags [thereof] upon the around, by reason of pride. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">فُضُولُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغَنَائِمِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The remains of the spoils when they are divided</hi> (TA;) such as a single horse, or a single camel (KL.)                   <foreign lang="ar">فضول</foreign>, a word which is here of uncertain meaning,] is thus explained: Háshim and Zuhrah and Teym [accord. to the CK Teymà] went in to 'Abd-Allah Ibn-Jud'án, and united in a confederacy to repel wrongdoing, and to exact the due from the wrongdoer; and it was thus called because they bound themselves by their confederacy not to leave in the possession of any one aught remaining [of property] whereof he aught despond any one, without their taking it for him [i. e. the latter] from him [i. e. the former] (O, K, TA: [in the CK, <foreign lang="ar">يَظْلِمُهُ أَحَدٌ</foreign> is a mistake for <foreign lang="ar">يظلمه</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدًا</foreign>:]) or it was thus called as being likened to a confederacy, or covenant, which was made of old, at Mekkeh, in the days of Jurhum, to act with mutual equity, and to take for the weak from the strong, and for the stranger from the resident, and in which three men, every one of whom was named El-Fadl, joined: and it was also called that of the <foreign lang="ar">مَطَيَّبُون</foreign>. (TA. [See art. <foreign lang="ar">طيب</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  The saying <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَمْلِكُ دِرْهَمًا فَضْلًا عَنْ دِينَارٍ</foreign>, and the like may be said of other sayings similar to it, means <hi rend="ital">He does not possess a dirhem nor a deenár</hi> [or rather <hi rend="ital">much less a deenár</hi>]: it is as though one said, <hi rend="ital">he does not possess a dirhem: how then should he possess a deenár?</hi> for the negation of that which is much is a necessary consequence of the negation of that which is little: <foreign lang="ar">فَضْلًا</foreign> is here in the accus case as an inf. n.; the implied meaning being <foreign lang="ar">فَقَدَ مِلْكَ دِرْهَمٍ فَقْدًا</foreign> 
                  <pb n="2413"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَفْضُلُ عَنْ فَقْدِ مِلْكِ دينَارٍ</foreign> [or rather <foreign lang="ar">يَفْقِدُ</foreign> &amp;c., i. e. <hi rend="ital">he lacks the possession of a dirhem with a lacking exceeding the lacking of the possession of a deenár</hi>]: (Msb:) Kutb-ed-Deen Esh-Sheerázee says, (Msb, TA,) in the Expos. of the “ Miftáh, ” (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">فَضْلًا</foreign> is used in a case in which the inferior [of two things] is deemed a thing of which the existence is improbable, and the impossibility of the existence of a thing that is above it is meant thereby; wherefore it occurs between two phrases differing in meaning; and it is mostly used after a particle of negation: (Msb, TA:) AHei says that he had not found any authority for it in the [classical] language of the Arabs. (Msb. [See also <foreign lang="ar">بَلْهَ</foreign>, which is used in a somewhat similar manner.])    </entryFree>2b:T4c8,<entryFree id="n34081" key="فُضُلٌ" type="main">
